<Review>After an Extremely Bad experience on Sunday 02/14/2021, I was Never going back to this location even though it was about minutes away from my home! However, I submitted a complaint online through the company's website and to my surprise the following day I was contacted by a JITB representative by the name of Priscila.
I explained to Priscila the details of what happened that night. I explained to her that it was not my first time at this location and that Usually the staff is Very Helpful and Friendly. However, that night this was not the case. I told her that upon placing my order at the drive-thru I asked the person taking the order to Please Not place ice in the drink. I had been experiencing flu-like symptoms and I thought the ice Would worsen this. When I arrived to the window to pay, the young lady by the name of "Teresa" (I know this b/c that was the name on the receipt) handed the drink to me. I Immediately noticed it had ice and Politely told her that I had asked for the drink with No Ice. What she stated next not only shocked me but it Extremely upset me as well. She stated "Well you should have told me when you placed the order!" Her manner was like she was scolding Me and she actually seemed upset for those couple of seconds.
I then stated to her that I Did let her know that I asked for No Ice in the drink. At No point did this young lady even take the time to apologize for a simple mistake. THAT to me was Even More upsetting! So I asked her for her name, to which she RUDELY replied "It's On The Receipt!" I then asked if her manager was available, to which she replied "I Am the manager." I asked her if she could please give me the name and number of her district manager and she again, stated yet Even More upset, "You can look it up online!"
I was Extremely Shocked and UPSET so I decided to place the formal complaint on the company's website. I would Definitely recommend this location to friends and family however, if something doesn't seem right then let it be known. 02/06/21
Sad to see that Pho Craft is gone. The owners were very nice, friendly and excellent chefs. I will miss their food and company. I wish them the best and hope they give it another try when we get past the current situation.

05/17/20
Update from the staff at Pho Craft:

We are happy to announce that we are open for take out orders beginning Monday, May 18th.

Our current Store Hours
Monday-Saturday: 11:00 am - 8:00 pm
Sunday: Closed

12/19
The House Special Pho was highly recommended and I can see why. The broth is rich and has a depth of flavor that reflects the use of cooking the soup with the bones for hours. We had a chance to speak to the chef who described how she makes the broth. No wonder it tastes so good.

Delicious food and friendly staff. Just a nice place to have a good meal. Prices are very reasonable.< /text>

<UserId.>102416785510177314476<//UserId.>< username>
Vincent Nguyen<//username>
< date>
1618782269689< /date>
<rate>3<//rate>< review>
I stayed for four days here. Arrive before 10pm or be locked out despite having a gate code (reservations). I had to rent a hotel the first night as the ca.reservation.gov website made no distinction between a closed gate with code lock, versus a locked gate with hard time of entry. The code was effectively useless.

So be sure to arrive before 10pm.

I easily spent 100$ to not sleep in my car at the local motel the first night. It was better than the campground or never falling asleep in my car.. but it over doubled my renting expenses in a single night. Also, bring a n95 mask for the porta-potties, as the normal public bathrooms are closed off.

Area is lush in grass and walking trails are alright though privacy is near non-existent. Many campsites were empty despite the foot traffic. I always had another human in my peripheral vision during my time there, let alone earshot. Area seems to be a magnet for folks who just want to throw a frat party in the woods; enough noise to drown out the local birds fighting on the riverside from 9pm to 11pm.

Mosquitoes are a consistent nuisance out there but I did not encounter hornets as others describe when I started grilling or prepping.

Camp host was polite and drives by your campsite on golf cart; at least makes a round of the sites about 4-5 times a day to my witness. I would definitely visit on a day trip for the shore, but I will pass on staying the night again.</review>

< rate>
1</rate>
<text>It's extremely open and feels more like a day use picnic area than a campground. It's in a young grove of oak trees that provide a decent amount of shade but no privacy. Campsites are practically on top of each other. The bathrooms are locked and you need a code to enter. They were clean the first day we got here but after 3 days, they have not been cleaned or restocked. There are flush toilets and coin operated showers and roaches in the sinks.

It's dog friendly and I've had no complaints about my 4 dogs but they definitely need to be leashed here. There are tons of ground squirrels that drive the dogs crazy and their holes in the ground make walking around challenging. There are also tons of flies and wasps. Dont plan on cooking here, we were swarmed by wasps as soon as we took our camp stove out every time. The camp host is also rude and unwelcoming, asking us multiple times about our reservations and how long we are staying. He and the park ranger seem to be buddies and drive around all day eyeing you down.

Okay spot to sleep in a pinch or if you have an RV. I would not stay here again.< /text><pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPeoPnLRBzlZ0jNfxPlD8WUVdfDqgRCZhrfrx1B=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOnRa3AC6AoyoY7kskivR2ql9gNQbMf6rYbNjPP=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOMjO83rw0872FUpumDSjYiMF_x3oApp7VIXXks=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipO8C3uotdAUAjd3sSB6w8BM2FKqVHcutTHF8qiq=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]</pics>< Response>

<review>The campground itself is nice aside from mostly smaller sites and not too much privacy. The trees are beautiful, lots of grass, and it's close to the river. There are trails to hike.

The downside is the noise from outside of the campground. There's some kind of industrial building close by and there a noise like a jackhammer in the distance, all day and night, every 5 seconds (literally). The train also passes through nearby a couple times per night.

Price: standard tent: $16. Electric and water: $25. Group site: $30. As of mid-September.

Bathrooms: clean, one has dry toilets and the other has flush toilets with quarter-operated showers.

While I wouldn't stay here for a weekend (due to the noise) it was fine for a place to stop for the night while passing through. You can bring some earplugs. :)</review><Time>1473693740076< /Time><user>113133628803642425505</user>< gmap_id>

< Review>
Sadly, this has become a less-than desirable spot in the past couple of years. Although it is a beautiful campground along the Sacramento River, it has become mostly a place for homeless folks to live. They game the reservation system so they never leave, just move from campsite to campsite. Very few spaces occupied by folks passing thru, like us. The camp host doesn't really seem to care, or has no power, not sure which.</Review>

<name>sam punter< /name>< text>
Far enough from the interstate to be fairly quiet. Showers have combination lock the host occasionally changes the combination to. Some sites have electricity, most don't Most sites are well shaded. Beautiful, clear Sacramento River is a stone's throw away and there is access. In addition to the host, there is also a Forest Service post at the south end of the campground. So it's well patrolled. The nature center at the entrance has displays of local wildlife, fish migration, etc. There's also a native plant nursery next to it with plants labeled. The reserve you drive through on way to the campground (a dead-end road) has trails where I saw two bucks and a do standing in the meadow. Lots of rare birds. Watch for snakes if you hike around though. Fortunately this jewel is close to the town of Red Bluff so if there is any need for emergency service, it's right there. All in all a beautiful nature preserve on the upper Sacramento River. Some terrific bike trails- the kids will love it.< /text>

103524066118409307693<//UserId.>
<Name>YLesaMarie</Name>< Time>
1611365959365<//Time>
<Rate>3<//Rate>< Text>
*Please like!

Nice place to camp in Red Bluff, Mendocino National Forest. The campsites are all on the grass, some under trees but there's not much separating each site from another. So if your neighbor's are noisy or have a bunch of kids then you will hear them.

There's a fire pit, BBQ and picnic table for each site. Some sites have hookups for water and electricity for an extra fee.

Regular campsites are $16 and can only be paid online with a debit or credit card through Recreation.Gov.

They DO NOT accept CASH here.

There is an onsite host 24/7 who is a little rough around the edges but overall is pretty good at communicating with campers and keeping the grounds maintained.

Bathrooms for men and women w/showers .25 for 4 minutes.
Hot and cold water.

The river is close by and boat launch. There are a couple of trails to walk and check out all of the neat birds that migrate to the area. We found some awesome wild blackberries growing along the paths.

It is very hot all day and all night. We stayed in July. It is definitely not a place to camp to get away from people but it is nice if you want to mingle with other campers. DOGS are welcome.</Text>

This is a local jewel of a resource for enjoying camping at a national park in our own back yard. From the well maintained facilities to the diligent staff, we are blessed to have this campground in our town. From camping out to going fishing or Taking your boat out, this has it all.  Free parking and boat ramps and clean restrooms, a souvenir shop, the camp ground has bathrooms and coin operated showers that last long enough to finish before the water shuts off. Fire pits, you can throw up a tent or bring a fifth wheel, and while there's a little life when the campfires roar and your enjoying your favorite barbecue, it gets real peaceful and beatiful especially on a star filled night. <user_id>116644304034580180213< /user_id><username>Martin Batistelli<//username><date>1472665072027< /date><Rate>4< /Rate>< Review>
Very serene and quiet. A park-like setting next to the decommissioned Red Bluff Diversion Dam and fish ladder on the Sacramento River. There were not many campers on the day we were there (Tuesday/Wednesday). There is a garden with native plants and a visitor center staffed with very friendly people next to the campground. The only downside is the constant hiss of a vaccum release from the paper mill across the river every 5 seconds (really, I timed it).<//Review>

Sycamore grove is the worst campground i have ever camped at.in fact its not even a campground,its more of a dayuse park that was converted into a campground and is definitely not worth the 16$ a night.
Lets start with the campsite itself.the sites here are so small that your basically 2 feet from all neighboring campsites which gives you no privacy at all.the sites are filthy ( my firepit was full of fast food containers and cigarette butts dirty bandaids) and theres so many wasps, bees,and flies that make it impossible to cook anything at your site without being constantly attacked by bugs.the bathrooms here are locked with a number code that your not given in the conformation reciept and so your forced to ask the fat hillbilly redneck host to give you the code as he gives you dirty looks.bathrooms are disgusting and only cleaned by the lazy slobs that work here once a week.there is also no soap in the bathroom.
The host that works here is very unwelcoming and does absolutely nothing all day but ride around on a golf cart harrassing the campers.last night at 8pm the host rudely rolls up in a golf cart shining lights all over my site asking me for my conformation receipt for the second time in one stay. The host is a bored loser that instead of cleaning and filling the large holes allover the property created by moles digging up the ground,hes standing there with the 3 other rednecks that work here talking loudly and setting off sprinklers for 2 hours straight.
Long story short,the scumbag host and his wife act like these campgrounds are their property in their backyard,do and work on absolutely nothing,live there for free and hate when campers come to use the sites.the way this host is living here for free and abusing the position of host makes me sick. Looked like a decent park. But the 'RESERVATIONS ONLY' billboard that greeted us upon entry in the end drove us away. As full-time Rver's (12 years) we stay in a lot of Federal Parks, mostly USFS and COE. We rarely make reservations. At Sycamore Grove (ignoring the silly sign) we pulled into a site that read 'OPEN', and walked around the park to meet the hosts, per instructions for those arriving without reservations. There we were told that despite being parked in a 'open' site, and despite the fact that the campground was pretty much empty, we had to call in a 'reservation' and pay a $10 fee.to do so. Plus the fee for our site; $22 I think it was. But by then it didn't matter. We left and moved to a private campground in town.< /Review>
